## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator. The acceleration dv_dt is determined by restoring forces (functions of x), damping forces (functions of v), and possibly external driving forces (functions of t). Nonlinearity introduces higher-order polynomial or transcendental terms beyond the simple linear -¤ë┬▓x.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator (unforced): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + linear damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * x**2 * v (nonlinear damping)
- Driven harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (periodic external force)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (full Duffing with driving)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * Abs(x) (asymmetric nonlinear restoring force)
- Nonlinear damping with cubic velocity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity damping)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * cos(c1 * t) (time-modulated stiffness)
- Mathieu-Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * cos(c2 * t) + c3 * x**3 (parametric + nonlinear)
- General polynomial oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v + c4 * v * x**2 (mixed polynomial terms)
- Sinusoidal restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (pendulum-like nonlinearity)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ÔåÆ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ÔåÆ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ÔåÆ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ÔåÆ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ÔåÆ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Symmetric restoring potential ÔåÆ only odd powers of x appear (x, x┬│, xÔüÁ) in the acceleration equation
- Amplitude-dependent frequency (nonlinear resonance) ÔåÆ cubic or higher odd-power terms in x (Duffing-type x┬│)
- Self-sustained oscillations ÔåÆ velocity-dependent terms with sign change, e.g., (c0 + c1*x┬▓)*v indicating energy injection at small amplitude and dissipation at large amplitude
- Parametric excitation ÔåÆ products of x with periodic functions of t, such as x*cos(c*t)
- Phase-space symmetry (invariance under xÔåÆ-x, vÔåÆ-v) ÔåÆ only odd-degree monomials in combined (x,v) variables
- Limit cycle behavior ÔåÆ nonlinear damping terms like x┬▓*v or v┬│ that balance energy input/output
- Pendulum-like large-angle effects ÔåÆ sin(c*x) replacing linear x, capturing periodic potential wells
- External periodic forcing ÔåÆ pure functions of t (sin/cos) appearing as additive terms independent of x and v
